## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, a core problem in materials science and solid mechanics. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus and introduces thermal softening or thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally-activated softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (flow stress with strain hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial modulus with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with temperature effect)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon**c1) * (T**c2) (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T**c2) (multiplicative thermal degradation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → multiplicative factor on strain: f(T) * epsilon, where f(T) is linear, polynomial, or exponential in T
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress at large strains
- Thermal softening → multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^m) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at high temperature
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and nonlinear term (epsilon^n) capturing yield and hardening
- Separable temperature-strain coupling → sigma = g(epsilon) * h(T), where stress factorizes into independent strain and temperature functions
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 for work-hardening metals (Hollomon-type)
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 accounts for initial yield offset in Swift-type models
- Polynomial stress-strain → c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon^2 + c2*epsilon^3 for rubber-like or hyperelastic materials

**GT:** `11.11905*epsilon**2 + 11.11905*epsilon*(-0.09196*(T - 352.008) + 1) + 4.3699*(T - 352.008)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me first expand the GT:
- `11.11905*epsilon**2 + 11.11905*epsilon*(-0.09196*T + 0.09196*352.008 + 1) + 4.3699*(T - 352.008)*log(epsilon + 1)`
- `= 11.11905*epsilon**2 + 11.11905*epsilon*(-0.09196*T + 33.373) + 4.3699*T*log(epsilon+1) - 4.3699*352.008*log(epsilon+1)`
- `= 11.11905*epsilon**2 + (-1.0224*T + 371.11)*epsilon + 4.3699*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1538.2*log(epsilon+1)`

So the GT has these structural terms:
1. `epsilon**2` term (constant coefficient)
2. `T*epsilon` term (linear in both)
3. `epsilon` term (constant coefficient)
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` term
5. `log(epsilon+1)` term (constant coefficient)

Now I need to find a candidate that can produce all these terms. The key structural requirement is having both `T*log(epsilon+1)` and `log(epsilon+1)` terms, plus `epsilon**2`, `T*epsilon`, and `epsilon`.

**Candidate 23:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon*log(T*c6 + 1) + c7*epsilon**2/T**(1/3)`

This has `log(c4*epsilon+1)` (good for the log term) but with constant coefficient, not `T*log(...)`. The `epsilon*log(T*c6+1)` term has wrong functional form - it's `epsilon*log(T)` not `T*log(epsilon)`. This doesn't match.

**Candidate 64:** `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c1 + c5*exp(T*c6)*log(c7*epsilon + 1)`

Setting c1=1: `T*c0*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*log(c7*epsilon+1)`
Setting c3=2: `T*c0*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2 + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6)*log(c7*epsilon+1)`

The term `exp(T*c6)*log(c7*epsilon+1)` — if c6 is small, this approximates `(1+T*c6)*log(...)` but it's exponential, not linear in T. This can't exactly match `T*log(epsilon+1) + const*log(epsilon+1)`.

**Candidate 22:** `c0*exp(T*c1) + c2*epsilon**c3*exp(T*c1) + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*exp(T*c7)*log(c8*epsilon + 1)`

**Candidate 125:** `c0*exp(T*c1) + c2*epsilon**c3*exp(T*c1) + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7`

**Candidate 36:** `T*c0*epsilon + T**c1*c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**c3`

**GT:** `11.119*epsilon**2 + 11.119*epsilon*(-0.0920*(T - 352.008) + 1) + 4.370*(T - 352.008)*log(epsilon + 1)`

- `= 11.119*epsilon**2 - 1.023*T*epsilon + 371.1*epsilon + 4.370*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1538.3*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon**2` (coefficient ~11.119)
2. `T*epsilon` (coefficient ~-1.023)

4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` (coefficient ~4.370)

Now I need to find candidates that can express exactly these 5 basis functions.

Let me check candidates systematically. I need candidates with terms: `epsilon**2`, `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, and `log(epsilon+1)`.

**Candidate 23:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon*log(T*c6 + 1) + c7*epsilon**2/T**(1/3)`

This has: `T*epsilon` ✓, `epsilon` ✓, `epsilon**2` ✓, `log(c4*epsilon+1)` ✓, `epsilon*log(T*c6+1)` ✗ (not `T*log(epsilon+1)`), `epsilon**2/T^(1/3)` ✗

The term `epsilon*log(T*c6+1)` is NOT the same as `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are fundamentally different functions.

This is a critical distinction. The GT needs `T*log(epsilon+1)`, but many candidates have `epsilon*log(T*c + 1)`. These are NOT equivalent.
